<div id="review_714360839" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/714360839" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/714360839?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062087973" href="/book/show/11181750-the-summer-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=cheaters">cheaters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=emotional-angsty-books">emotional-angsty-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer714360839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12208749537778332437">4.5 ★'s<br/><br/>So if you've read the blurb, you know that now Alexander and Tatiana are finally reunited and in America. Unfortunately, not all their problems are solved. They both have changed so much in their time apart and they are parents now...trying to find a way to make their family and their lives work. <br/><br/>I was sooo <i>happy</i> when I started reading this book and finally got to the parts I've been waiting for..Shura and Tania back together! I have to admit that I'm a little upset that we didn't get the</span>
  <span id="freeText12208749537778332437" style="display:none">4.5 ★'s<br><br>So if you've read the blurb, you know that now Alexander and Tatiana are finally reunited and in America. Unfortunately, not all their problems are solved. They both have changed so much in their time apart and they are parents now...trying to find a way to make their family and their lives work. <br><br>I was sooo <i>happy</i> when I started reading this book and finally got to the parts I've been waiting for..Shura and Tania back together! I have to admit that I'm a little upset that we didn't get the big reunion with Anthony...WTH? And I would've liked to have some story about how Alexander felt about New York especially because as you read further in the story, it's very obvious he has some issues with it. <br><br>They've decided to buy a camper and move from place to place staying a month at each location and getting to see and know America. Usually they ended up staying way longer than a month and for the most part that was a good thing. Of course, there were some problems though.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/668603.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alexander is pretty messed up and luckily Tania doesn't let up working her "magic" to get him back to his old self. Alexander also has to insert himself into Anthony's life and become his Dad which is a little hard because he's been so used to Tania. Tania also ends up keeping a huge secret from Alexander and that causes a lot of unnecessary drama. <br><br>Finally, they end up at the property that Tania bought with Alexander's mother's money in Arizona. I was really surprised that they ended up living here because Alexander seemed so against it. But things started coming together for them. Alexander finding something that he enjoyed doing and Tania nursing. Unfortunately, still more red flags! <br><br>And then...well, you knew it was coming but it's just sooo heart breaking! And to be honest, I felt it was very out of character for Shura. I get his reasons but they were flimsy at best and heck, I can even understand the first part but the car and especially then the Wednesday <i>and his best suit!!</i>...horrible, just horrible. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/606701.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then....it's the big blow up! I had a hard time with how women were treated during that time period and while certainly Tania doesn't hold her punches, I was totally shocked at what Shura did. I think I might be more upset with him about this....naw, they're both really, really bad.<br><br>But I do love all that drama...it literally made the book and in a weird way, it cemented their relationship even more. Sadly, after this, it became a big snoozefest for me. I just don't like all that military stuff and I could care less about all the names of the different weapons. *BIG YAWN* The actually mission was good and the twist regarding Anthony was a big surprise for me. <br><br>The book ends with a sort of very long epilogue. The time has fast forwarded very quickly and we get caught up on what everyone is doing. It was a bit hard to keep track of who was who but I liked how things seem to come full circle especially the part where Shura and Tania were in town. (But what the heck was up with the mobile home?) <br><br>Overall, I enjoyed the series very much....definitely an epic love story. However, there are things that are too realistic and not realistic enough. There are things left unsaid and unanswered and then there are things that we find out too much about. We get Shura's POV when I want Tania's POV and vice versa. It's hard not to be picky when something affects you as much as this series does. I wish I could say more and talk about <i>all</i> the things I want to but those are spoilers! One way or another, this series will affect you...it's hard to quit thinking about it and even dreaming about it. Definitely a series that will be one of my favorites for a long, long time. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/597128.gif" width="400" height="050" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Favorite quotes:<br><br>♥ "Shh…Tatiasha…shh…I’m looking at you…and what do you know, it turns out that blonde…is my favorite color.”<br><br>♦ “Dad, why are they showing us their boobies?”<br><br>“I’m not sure, son. It’s a strange ritualistic custom common to these parts of the world.”<br><br>♥ “Are You a Match Made in Heaven, Crabby Cancer Girl and Chatty Gemini Guy?” (“They got us all wrong, Shura, didn’t they? It’s so the other way around.”)<br><br>♥ “And what kind does my own wife like?” <br><br>“I like,” she said, grinning back through the mirror, “the baddest boy of all.”<br><br>♥ <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Iq0XJCJ1Srw" rel="nofollow noopener">Shura &amp; Tania's song</a> ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="12208749537778332437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="*on hiatus*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5058045-on-hiatus"><img alt="*on hiatus*" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103898433?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="*on hiatus*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="*on hiatus*" href="/user/show/5058045-on-hiatus">*on hiatus*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103898433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1669818032977122013">ALL THE STARS. <br/><br/>So it´s been weeks since I finished The Summer Garden and I haven´t been been able to write this review at all. But why? You ask. What in the world is going on with you? This is your favorite romance of all time. After all, this is Shura we are talking about... Shura with the sled and the copy of Pushkin and Shura with the creme-brulee eyes and delicious tanned skin with that faint scent of nicotine in the morning after endless bouts of hot Lazarevo sex. Didn´t you love this book </span>
  <span id="freeText1669818032977122013" style="display:none">ALL THE STARS. <br /><br />So it´s been weeks since I finished The Summer Garden and I haven´t been been able to write this review at all. But why? You ask. What in the world is going on with you? This is your favorite romance of all time. After all, this is Shura we are talking about... Shura with the sled and the copy of Pushkin and Shura with the creme-brulee eyes and delicious tanned skin with that faint scent of nicotine in the morning after endless bouts of hot Lazarevo sex. Didn´t you love this book and rate it ALL THE STARS in the universe? What is wrong with you? <br /><br />Well, this freaking trilogy is what is wrong with me. Shura wrecked me and now I can't recover. I have spent the last few weeks thinking about this book, getting my hands on as many WW2 wartime romance movies and shows as I can, scouring the internet for recommendations on what to read after this trilogy. And now I come here defeated, head down because, alas, seems like I'm screwed. I wish someone had warned me this series was going to ruin all other romance novels for me. <br /><br />Like, for real people, who is going to compare to Alexander Barrington? Jamie Fraser you say. Read Outlander, you say. Well, I already read Outlander, Dragonfly in Amber and Voyager years ago and while I enjoyed them very much - Outlander is one of my favorite romance novels of all time after all - let's face it. It's no TBH. Fellow Alexander lovers will understand what I'm talking about. I want Shura in the tent and the cabin in Lazarevo levels of epic romance. That's what I want. I want Tatia with the Red Cross, in the wolves den of the Sachsenhausen Prison Camp trying to hide the emotions ravaging her insides levels of epic angst. I mean, if you don't have potato shelf levels of hotness, I don't know what to tell you.<br /><br />So I'm going to turn this review, which let's face it, I'm doing an awful job of actually reviewing The Summer Garden, into a desperate plea for recommendations on what to do with my life reading-wise post TBH. I can't pay you, but you'll be doing the Lord's work. I've heard whispers of other books out there, like the Tea Rose series by Jennifer Donnely and The Pillars of the Earth by Ken Follet, or Florencia Bonelli's Year of Fire trilogy. I just don't know, guys. I kind of just want to go reread The Bronze Horseman. I already read From Sand and Ash earlier this year and although a worthy contender, TBH is still better.<br /><br />Just a quick note regarding The Summer Garden because I will feel guilty if I don't actually touch upon the actual story. No, it did not ruin Alexander for me. Was I close to bitch-slapping the ever loving life out of him (virtually speaking) more than once in the book? Oh hell yes. Not so much for that thing with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Carmen, although that WAS cheating... not gross unforgivable cheating. It's not like any part of him went inside her unmentionable orifices, but it was nasty cheating nonetheless. Why, oh why did he have to suck her tits, amirite, and let that hoebag suck his dick? Jesus hell. I thought I already wanted to kill him when he went to that strip joint. But I feel that the thing with this trilogy, and what I personally love so much, is that it feels so realistic. It's not a rosy, safe, predictable romance with heroes that feel like robotic concoctions straight off the flowery pink mind of a romance novelist. Alexander is raw, and real and fiery. And as such, I respect the gruesome earthy view of the real challenges a couple like Tatiana and Alexander would face in the middle of the macho-centric culture dominating the 50s. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />So no, it wasn't that particular issue that threatened to ruin my love for my Shura, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The fact he hit her. Oh boy, that made me reel. And he was going to do it again had Anthony not made a timely appearance. Unforgivable yes, but considering the scope of this book and how it spans their entire lifetimes, this horrible chapter is forgiven in my book by sole virtue that it WAS a one-time thing. I had more problems with how the baby seemed to come along at just the perfect time and how it seems their marriage would have gone downhill faster than you can say potato shelf had it not been for that pregnancy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />That ending did a number in my heart. Damn you, Paullina Simons. Oh, and there was a surprising amount of sex in this one. Guess who you'll find complaining? Yep, not me. <br /><br />Also, I'm going to need a Napa-sized, brothel bed. <br /><br />And just one more tidbit. It still surprises me how few people realize what The Bronze Horseman is really about. This book is really about Communism vs. the free world. Take Communist Russia out of it and you've got nothing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1669818032977122013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3242921015818068681"><i> “We thought the hard part was over—but we were wrong. Living is the hardest part. Figuring out how to live your life when you’re all busted up inside and out—there is nothing harder.” </i> <br/><br/>Read from June 17 to 24, 2012<br/>I just finished and it was AMAZING. I can't stop thinking about it. I just cried and cried at the end. I had to explain to my husband. LOL. <br/>I absolutely loved it. A total emotional rollercoaster but so real and so worth it. Paullina Simons is just so gifted with words. <br/><br/>I loved how in </span>
  <span id="freeText3242921015818068681" style="display:none"><i> “We thought the hard part was over—but we were wrong. Living is the hardest part. Figuring out how to live your life when you’re all busted up inside and out—there is nothing harder.” </i> <br /><br />Read from June 17 to 24, 2012<br />I just finished and it was AMAZING. I can't stop thinking about it. I just cried and cried at the end. I had to explain to my husband. LOL. <br />I absolutely loved it. A total emotional rollercoaster but so real and so worth it. Paullina Simons is just so gifted with words. <br /><br />I loved how in the second book, Tatiana and Alexander, you got flashbacks and insight into Alexander and what forged him growing up and then with The Summer Garden you get the same for Tatiana. You get to read more about her and what made her into who she is. And you also learn right along with Alexander that she is the strongest, bravest, least naive person you'd ever meet despite her diminutive size. <br /><br />This book is probably the hardest in Tatiana and Alexander's journey, but it is real. It captures all the hardship and ugliness of trying your best to live your life and recover from war and all its atrocities. This book will hit you where you live. This book will give you laughter, tears and total heartbreak and if you survive till the end you will be rewarded with the gift of the best ending you could ever hope for. <br /><br />The end of this book brought the story full circle for me and it felt like I got the prize at the bottom of the cereal box. I love sitting and imagining Alexander and his "I'll-get-on-the-bus-for-you-anytime face". It makes my heart swell and my eyes get misty. <br /><br />I would read this series over and over and over. I just don't want to say goodbye to these characters. <br /><br />January 26, 2013<br />Update: Just finished this for the second time. I have a few things to add to my original review but overall nothing has really changed. This was an amazing emotional roller coaster and I loved it. Although <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The scenes after that bitch Carmen were even WORSE the second time around. I think it's because I knew it was coming. I felt sick and dreaded every second. I sobbed as they had it out. I felt like my stomach was being scraped with a rusty knife and it was awful.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This book answers the question everyone has at the end of every love story. What happened next? Books 1 and 2 were about the love and this book was about their LIFE. Every heartbreaking, tear-jerking, scream inducing second of it was worth it for the ending. <br /><br />3rd re-read January 12, 2014 - January 19, 2014 - LOVED LOVED LOVED</span>

  <span id="freeText13967914062896662388" style="display:none">This conclusion to The Bronze Horseman series, which I have been reading for years, was perfect.   <span id="freeText17792720276857177769" style="display:none"><b>The spectacular, emotional conclusion to my all-time favorite love story! Exhaustingly intense. Piercingly agonizing. Achingly beautiful. Enduringly romantic. I FELT EVERY MOMENT. INFINITY STARS!!!!!</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“To cross the street. To follow her. And she will give your life meaning, she will save you. Yes, yes-to cross.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>How does one get past this series? How can you even begin to compare other love stories to the one of Tatiana and Alexander? You just cannot, I think. The three books will forever sit on a shelf all their own, for what they imparted is an unforgettable story of love and survival… come what may.<br><br>Book 3, The Summer Garden, is quite different from book 2, which is different from book 1. Each book tells a unique part of their story, of their struggles, of their love. The Bronze Horseman is about Tatiana and Alexander coming together, believing their love is real, unstoppable, forever… alive and burning despite war and starvation. Book 2, Tatiana and Alexander, is about fiercely fighting fate and finding each other in a sea of impossible circumstances… it’s about being relentless and unforgiving in your pursuit of happiness. The Summer Garden is a tough read. It’s about survival, but this time it’s not only about surviving war, it’s about surviving time, change, insecurities, pride, betrayal… and all without giving up when it all just seems like too much to bear. Sometimes, I think it’s almost easier to survive something tangible like war or hunger, than something as deeply cutting and intangible as a broken heart. A disappointed heart. An angry heart. Matters of the heart consume voraciously, tilting the world on its axis until you don’t know what’s wrong and what’s right… where the blurry line solidifies to become one moment too many to keep enduring before calling it quits. Or is there really an uncrossable line when it comes to your soul mate?<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Where was he, her Alexander, of once? Was he truly gone? The Alexander of the Summer Garden, of their first Lazarevo days, of the hat in his hands, white toothed, peaceful, laughing, languid, stunning Alexander, had he been left far behind?<br>Well, Tatiana supposed that was only right.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>For Alexander believed his Tatiana of once was gone, too. The swimming child Tatiana of the Luga, of the Neva, of the River Kama.<br>Perhaps on the surface they were still in their twenties, but their hearts were old.”<br><br>Coming back from the pulse-pumping experience of Alexander’s almost life-claiming liberation, I felt an overwhelming sense of relief. But that feel-good feeling quickly vanishes as we realize that Alexander struggles to adjust to civilian life, retreating into himself and becoming a hard, cold, callous person.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“His eyes, once like caramel, were now hard copper, nothing liquid or flowing in them. He turned his polite face to hear, and she turned her polite face back. He wanted quiet, she gave him plenty. He wanted to go for a walk, she was ready. He wanted newspapers, magazines, cigarettes, she brought them all. He wanted to sit mutely in his chair; she sat mutely on the ground by his side. Anything he wanted, she was ready at any moment to give him.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>For me, being so invested in their relationship, this part of the book was really painful and heartbreaking to read and it felt very REAL. Their closeness and intensity became a frigid façade… a widening chasm that continued to expand. This was a chasm widened by pride, insecurities, fear and even love, because if they didn’t love each other so ardently, they wouldn’t have shattered hearts. Their relationship thrived in the violent throes of war and the pressing intensity of their struggles, so suddenly, when they begin a new life in the quiet of everyday trifles, everything comes apart.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“That’s the chasm. You go through something that changes you. You see things you can’t unsee. Then you are sleepwalking through your actual life, shell-shocked.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Then, on top of that, their safety comes into question again, and the stress I thought I left behind in book 2 emerged again, and I was fearful that they were never going to have peace.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“What if this little life, us, is all just an illusion and will soon be gone.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>And then LIFE… FATE… continue to push and push and it all begins to unravel even after some possibly unforgivable choices. I felt so betrayed, crushed and saddened. I just FELT and FELT and FELT EVERYTHING. I found it quite interesting that at this point, I am SO deeply connected with these characters, so understanding of what they’ve been through, that I no longer saw their faults… I saw their humanity. I love Tatiana and Alexander… for every flaw, for their fighting spirit, for their fiercely stubborn love and even for their unwavering pride.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Alexander, you broke my heart. But for carrying me on your back, for pulling my dying sled, for giving me your last bread, for the body you destroyed for me, for the son you have given me, for the twenty-nine days we lived like Red Birds of Paradise, for all our Naples sands and Napa wines, for all the days you have been my first and last breath, for Orbeli- I will forgive you.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>The Summer Garden spans years, and you really see their life unfold moment by moment, year by year. Their memories were my memories… I LIVED IT. I FELT IT. I was so emotional during this book, so vulnerable, so impacted by everything that happened. I was a big, fat, ugly mess of tears the last 30% or so of the book and by the end I was sobbing. It’s incredibly difficult to summarize my thoughts on this book and the series, but there’s a few important things I want to impart. First off, the writing is stellar. Stunning. Amazing. Perfection. Poetic. Throw every praising adjective you can at it… it’s brilliant. Secondly, because of the writing, because of the story, I just FELT the entire series. I was deeply, emotionally moved… so much so, that I know for a fact that I will never forget this story. It’s an instant classic, belonging in the ranks of all the greats. Thirdly, Tatiana has become my favorite female character… her strength and selflessness is inspiring. I was in awe at her uncrushable spirit and her limitless capacity for love. Lastly, this is the most amazing love story ever told. What else can I say? I’m so sad to have come to the end of this experience… exhaustingly intense, piercingly agonizing, achingly beautiful and enduringly romantic. My all-time favorite series. Numero 1. A million bright, shining stars!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I don’t want this life to end,” said Alexander. “The good, the bad, the everything, the very old, to ever end.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381417425i/4836951._SX540_.png" width="361.33" height="228.67" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>For more reviews, connect with me: <br><a href="www.vilmasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Vilma's Book Blog</a> | <a href="www.facebook.com/chitchatbookblog" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="www.twitter.com/vilmairis" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17792720276857177769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5544829-donna?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300942683" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13634441277780421223">There were things I loved about this book and there were things I hated about this book, but in can all be wrapped up in one word that never fails to describe Tatiana & Alexander - Orbeli. They are each others most loved and treasured possession. Each other's purpose for living.<br/><br/>I loved seeing them trying to figure out the relationship & marriage they thought they would never have. I hated seeing them trying to figure it out as well. I hated that they were so insecure in each other yet so incredi</span>
  <span id="freeText13634441277780421223" style="display:none">There were things I loved about this book and there were things I hated about this book, but in can all be wrapped up in one word that never fails to describe Tatiana &amp; Alexander - Orbeli. They are each others most loved and treasured possession. Each other's purpose for living.<br /><br />I loved seeing them trying to figure out the relationship &amp; marriage they thought they would never have. I hated seeing them trying to figure it out as well. I hated that they were so insecure in each other yet so incredibly secure at the same time. They needed to talk to each and, more importantly, listen to each other. It took a pretty serious event to finally get them to pay attention to each other .... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ "Alexander, you broke my heart. But for carrying me on your back, for pulling my dying sled, for giving me your last bread, for the body you destroyed for me, for the son you have given me, for the twenty-nine days we lived like Red Birds of Paradise, for all our Naples sands and Napa wines, for all the days you have been my first and last breath, for Orbeli - I will forgive you. "  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In a perfect world that is all puppies &amp; rainbows &amp; unicorns, life for Tatiana &amp; Alexander would always be happy. However, we know that can't happen, but, what turns their life together takes are very real. Paullina Simons has written this story in a way that you cannot help but see everything so vividly. You are right there with them experiencing and feeling everything they are .. the good, the bad and the painful. <br /><br />This book had me holding my breath, laughing, sighing, panicking, gripping my Nook with fear, crying and loving every minute of it. <br /><br />I think all the books in this trilogy are exquisitely written. I treasure books that are written by someone whose words can pull me into the story and take me on a roller coaster of emotion that I don't ever want to end. I can 'like' a book, but to actually 'live' a book is what reading is all about for me.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14219487667711293864">“Shine on, shine on, my only star, <br/><br/>My star of love eternally,<br/><br/>You are my sole and chosen one,<br/><br/>There’ll be no other one for me…”<br/><br/> Again I am blown away by Paullinna Simon’s ability to destroy your heart, body and soul.   <span id="freeText14219487667711293864" style="display:none">“Shine on, shine on, my only star, <br /><br />My star of love eternally,<br /><br />You are my sole and chosen one,<br /><br />There’ll be no other one for me…”<br /><br /> Again I am blown away by Paullinna Simon’s ability to destroy your heart, body and soul. I was in such a distraught and emotional state after reading The Summer Garden the last book the The Bronze Horseman series. This woman is a goddess of worlds, a queen of stories.<br /><br />I loved that in this book we get to see a lot more of Tatiana childhood, and what she was really like before Alexander and what made her the way she was. I found myself really enjoying her so young, her family, her past. Which made me understand her and her action much better in this book. She was very loved, despite all that hate that was shown by her family in the first book. No mother or father loves one child more then the other, just differently. Oh how I liked Pasha…<br /><br />Tatiana and Alexander had many mountains of hell to climb before they found their bliss, their heaven. And while reading this book I felt that I was climbing that mountain right with them (which explain the state of my emotions at the end). But I’m so glad I’ve known them, I suffered with them, I was happy and loved by them. I felt that I had lived their life and at the end, I still had all my years to live mine. I have never been touched by a book this much. The Summer Garden will always be that book for me....<br /><br />I'll never be the same person after this series, never will I be able to forget the beautiful, difficult, sad, emotional, heartbreaking, strong and infinite love story that is Tatiana and Alexander. I was told that the most beautiful and most lovely love story, is also the hardest. You can not have the bliss of heaven without the suffering of hell. Now I truly believe it.<br /><br />MORE ABOUT THIS REVIEW IN MY BLOG...<br />viviheartbooks.worldpress.com<br /><br />;)</span>

<div id="review_1389672961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1389672961" />
    <a title="talon smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35885066-talon-smith"><img alt="talon smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603124377p2/35885066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1389672961?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="talon smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="talon smith" href="/user/show/35885066-talon-smith">talon smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1389672961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11461450640676139232">What the hell do I do with my life now? For the past month I have been so engrossed in these books, now that they are over I have no idea what to do with myself. The Summer Garden is the final book in the Bronze Horseman Trilogy. This final book (in my opinion) was set to a completely different pace than the first ones. In both the Bronze Horseman and Tatianna and Alexander there was love, betrayal, tragedy and hope all set against the backdrop of WWII. But in the Summer Garden, their story cont</span>
  <span id="freeText11461450640676139232" style="display:none">What the hell do I do with my life now? For the past month I have been so engrossed in these books, now that they are over I have no idea what to do with myself. The Summer Garden is the final book in the Bronze Horseman Trilogy. This final book (in my opinion) was set to a completely different pace than the first ones. In both the Bronze Horseman and Tatianna and Alexander there was love, betrayal, tragedy and hope all set against the backdrop of WWII. But in the Summer Garden, their story continues with their life after the war and it really delves into the characters and their day to day relationship. The author gives a very realistic portrayal of post war marriage and the obstacles they must overcome with their wartime past, inner demons, and outer conflicts. Also with adjusting to life outside of Russia.<br /><br />Since I was so invested in this book and in their relationship, it was really painful and heartbreaking to read it and it felt very REAL to me. Their closeness and intensity became very frigid. It felt like all of the tension could be cut with a butter knife. Their relationship had conquered the violent woes of war so when they begin a new life in the quiet of everyday trifles, everything comes apart. Why does it fall apart? What happened?<br /><br /><b>“That’s the chasm. You go through something that changes you. You see things you can’t unsee. Then you are sleepwalking through your actual life, shell-shocked.”</b><br /><br /><b>"I love you, I'm blind for you. I'm sick with you. Everything that happened to us, everything is because I crossed the street for you. I worship you. You know that through and through. The way I hold you, the way I touch you, my hands on you, God, me inside you, all the things I can't say during the daylight... Tatiana, Tania, Tatiasha, love, do you feel me?"</b><br /><br />As I got closer to end of this book my chest started to get heavy. My stomach had butterflies. And my palms were getting sweating. I felt an abundance of feelings. This book just encompassed me SO MUCH. I felt like I was in a vortex and I couldn't get out. It is realistic, it is emotional, it is full of pain, full of healing, which is just an on going theme I've accepted. It's not afraid to reach to the depth of you soul. Paullina holds nothing back in this one. She writes about human beings after all of their hurt and all of their struggle. But now that I'm finished I feel like I have just lost two best friends...<br /><br />...Until we meet again, Shura and Tania....<br />A kickass ending to a kickass saga.<br /><br />* full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.talonsbereadlist.wordpress.com">http://www.talonsbereadlist.wordpress...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11461450640676139232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_814058226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText16360718538496533743" style="display:none">I wish this book never existed.<br>I wish this book ended after first 30%. <br>I wish I never read it. <br><br>What happened?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391524332ra/8405156.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Where are the Tania and Shura I fell in love with? Where is the girl that was ready to put Alexander and her loved ones above everything else? Where is the loyal soldier? The one that worshiped her, the one that stood up to her father saying no one will ever raise a hand against her and hurt her ever again. <br><br>I feel cheated. It feels like I traveled from 1940s to 2000s and read a contemporary, screwed up version of my favorite epic love story. Tainted and poisoned with unnecessary drama. The essence of the characters and the foundation of their relationship gone. Stripped off their magic and epicness. I do understand why people say this storyline made this realistic. Yes, these are the struggles present in real life relationships. I just never thought this epic love would be challenged and almost defeated by such mundane obstacles. <br><br>The last drop of bitterness was the drama involving Anthony. That was just too much. Ridiculous. Skimmed through the last 30%. It felt dragged. <br><br>Summary of this book:<br>1-30% Painful but great conclusion to a beautiful series.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383507069ra/6581614.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>30-60% Bullshit.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391524497ra/8405187.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>60-70% More heartbreaking, unnecessary, out of character bullshit.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391524497ra/8405188.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>70-95% Ridiculous, dragged drama I skimmed through.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391516934ra/8403878.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>95-100% HEA. Way too much info I skimmed through.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391092220ra/8330187.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wish I could erase this book from my memory. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391524497i/8405189.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My last image of them would be Tania running into his arms while he says they are going home…<br><br><br></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11196760-the-summer-garden">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428900701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15399756120580610729"><a href='http://s1127.photobucket.com/albums/l630/speechnutt/?action=view&current=tumblr_mgmwkozrpS1qbm1qvo1_500_zps4853eb78.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380393486i/757587._SY540_.jpg' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Amazing!!!! If I could give this book 10 stars I would! </b><br/><br/>The Summer Garden is the final book in the epic Bronze Horseman Trilogy. This final installment was set to a different pace. In both the Bronze Horseman and Tatianna and Alexander, there was love, betrayal, tragedy and hope set against the backdrop of WWII. The action was intense as well as fast paced. In the Summer Garden, their story continues with life after the war and really delves into the characters and their day to day relations</span>
  <span id="freeText15399756120580610729" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1127.photobucket.com/albums/l630/speechnutt/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_mgmwkozrpS1qbm1qvo1_500_zps4853eb78.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380393486i/757587._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Amazing!!!! If I could give this book 10 stars I would! </b><br><br>The Summer Garden is the final book in the epic Bronze Horseman Trilogy. This final installment was set to a different pace. In both the Bronze Horseman and Tatianna and Alexander, there was love, betrayal, tragedy and hope set against the backdrop of WWII. The action was intense as well as fast paced. In the Summer Garden, their story continues with life after the war and really delves into the characters and their day to day relationship. The author gives a very realistic portrayal of post war marriage and the obstacles one must overcome with their wartime past, inner demons, and outer conflicts. The Summer Garden would not be complete without its unexpected, suprising twits in the plot that definitely keep the reader thoroughly engaged. It was far from predictable. I felt blind sided several times throughout the book. The author's character development, as always, was amazing! After reading all three books in the course of three weeks, I felt as though I really knew Tatianna and Alexander and felt all the love, joy, pain, and suffering these characters went through. Their love story was epic and one of the most beautiful I have personally ever read. <br><br><br><b> <i> <blockquote>"Shine on, shine on, my only star, my star of love eternally. You are my sole and chosen one. There will be no other one for me"<br>
</blockquote>
<br><br><a href="http://s1127.photobucket.com/albums/l630/speechnutt/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_lj4yigO8Hg1qiyepco1_500_zps60ebfd3b.png" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380393486i/757588.png" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br></i></b></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3007345-amira?shelf=love-story">love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3007345-amira?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79824237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2437602085687653298">I found the third book in the Bronze Horseman Trilogy,'The Summer Garden' disappointing. I really really really really LOVED the other two novels a lot, but this one departed too much from the characters that I had grown to love. I have to admit that most of the story was a collective extension of vague plotless prose, which didn't reflect the true essence of the characters Tatiana and Alexander. I also felt it lacked a climax and strongly disliked Alexander's indescretion and when he hit Tatian</span>
  <span id="freeText2437602085687653298" style="display:none">I found the third book in the Bronze Horseman Trilogy,'The Summer Garden' disappointing. I really really really really LOVED the other two novels a lot, but this one departed too much from the characters that I had grown to love. I have to admit that most of the story was a collective extension of vague plotless prose, which didn't reflect the true essence of the characters Tatiana and Alexander. I also felt it lacked a climax and strongly disliked Alexander's indescretion and when he hit Tatiana (that was not the true Shura I know and love), even Tatiana was mildly frustrating. Why couldn't they just talk to each other!!!! I couldn't get emotionally invested in the subplots, even with Anthony and Vikki etc. I ended up (ashamedly) skimming through most of it. I really wanted to love it, but I will only be actively recognising the first two books in the trilogy. Maybe I will revist this one when I have experience in a marriage and can relate more. The three stars are for Paullina Simons, I'm sorry.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2296112707" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer32721091985778153">This is the stunning conclusion to this epic love story that spanned over decades. There is so much raw emotion throughout this series and this final instalment had me in knots. I couldn’t sleep out of frustration and anger at times, the angst attacked me from all sides.<br/><br/>I loved all the rich history, stories like this open my eyes to things I know nothing about, the pain and suffering that people endured in times of war and after. The years of recovery to get back to some sort of semblance of a n</span>
  <span id="freeText32721091985778153" style="display:none">This is the stunning conclusion to this epic love story that spanned over decades. There is so much raw emotion throughout this series and this final instalment had me in knots. I couldn’t sleep out of frustration and anger at times, the angst attacked me from all sides.<br /><br />I loved all the rich history, stories like this open my eyes to things I know nothing about, the pain and suffering that people endured in times of war and after. The years of recovery to get back to some sort of semblance of a normal life.<br /><br />Love &amp; loyalty is challenged in this third book and that is where I felt the most frustrated. Things happened that I was not happy about and I felt the pain and sorrow as deeply as Tania and Alexander.<br /><br />The Vietnam War part of this book was incredibly intense and scary to read about so I can’t even imagine what it was like for real.<br /><br />And then the last part of the book was incredibly healing. It was like the author was rewarding me for sticking with this family and believing in them.<br /><br />I freaking LOVED this so much, the most beautiful true love story!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15707206509933379">This book has been in time out for two years. Two years !! I'm challenging myself to finish this by Dec 31st. I inhaled books 1 and 2 in November 2012 and immediately started this book. But then I came across a Shura that seemed foreign to me. So unless he had a come to Jesus with the quickness ~ I couldn't let my Shura fall from the pedestal. So I took a time-out and lived life pretending what THIS Shura did in THIS book didn't gut me. It's time to finish this epic series. Wish me luck ❤️</span>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review908546656">

<div id="review_739313103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739313103" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8278010-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352109855p2/8278010.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/739313103?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/8278010-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11196760-the-summer-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739313103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7360037060770357038"><br/><br/><b> 5++++ "UNFORGETTABLE, BEAUTIFUL,PAINFUL, EMOTIONAL, RAW, HEARTBREAKING, ENDEARING, ALL-CONSUMING,REAL AND TIMELESS STARS" </b><br/><br/><a href='http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/200/1cd9.jpg/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382658297i/6101236._SY540_.jpg' alt='Image Hosted by ImageShack.us' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I'm still at a loss of words to describe this series, to describe Tatiana and Alexander! I said it before but I'll say it again, there are love story and then there is Tania and Shura's story!<br/>Each and single book of this series moved me, enthralled me and made me live every single thing with them...and each book is so different in it's own way, each one is unique!<br/><br/><b>Summer </b></span>
  <span id="freeText7360037060770357038" style="display:none"><br><br><b> 5++++ "UNFORGETTABLE, BEAUTIFUL,PAINFUL, EMOTIONAL, RAW, HEARTBREAKING, ENDEARING, ALL-CONSUMING,REAL AND TIMELESS STARS" </b><br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/200/1cd9.jpg/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382658297i/6101236._SY540_.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I'm still at a loss of words to describe this series, to describe Tatiana and Alexander! I said it before but I'll say it again, there are love story and then there is Tania and Shura's story!<br>Each and single book of this series moved me, enthralled me and made me live every single thing with them...and each book is so different in it's own way, each one is unique!<br><br><b>Summer Garden</b> starts where most of the romance novels ends...it starts after the Tatia's and Shura reunion. They're now starting their life together with their little boy Ant. The possibilities seems endless now...they're free to live their life the way they want.<br>But the thing is they're not really free, they're away from Russia, from Germany but they aren't free of the horrors they suffered...especially Alexander, he have scars on the inside and on the outside that don't let him ever forget.<br><br><b>
  <i> "Does it hurt when I touch them?" He has to lie. Every kiss she plants on his wounds stirs a sense memory of how he got them. He wanted her to touch him, and this is what he gets. But if he tells her the truth, she will stop.So he lies. No,he says.</i>
</b><br><br>It's hard to meet this "new" Shura, this damaged Shura. He suffers from severe PTSD but he can't talk about it. He tries to move on the best he can, without soiling his wife and son.<br><br><b>
  <i>Then.Now. Eventually, he sees so much that he becomes dead to everything. He has inured himself, hardened himself so that there's nothing that arouses a flicker of feeling inside Alexander.</i>
</b><br><br>The other side is Tania, trying to figure it out how to reach him...how to take his demons and shadows away. She did the unthinkable and saved from the Gulac but is he really out from there?<br><br>So through this first years,they're traveling state to state, trying to find a home for themselves...but still hiding for each other all of what they're feeling.<br><br>We will be with them through all the hardships, struggles and victories. Sad, heartbreaking and emotional moments...<br><br><b>
  <i>“Alexander, you broke my heart. But for carrying me on your back, for pulling my dying sled, for giving me your last bread, for the body you destroyed for me, for the son you have given me, for the twenty-nine days we lived like Red Birds of Paradise, for all our Naples sands and Napa wines, for all the days you have been my first and last breath, for Orbeli- I will forgive you. ” </i>
</b><br><br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/42/byh.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382616890ra/6065268.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>...but also passionate and loving moments.<br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/35/y7e5.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382616970ra/6065418.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“I love you. I'm blind for you, wild for you. Sick with you. I told you that our first night together when I asked you to marry me, I am telling you now. Everything that's happened to us, everything, is because I crossed the street for you. I worship you. You know that through and through. The way I hold you, the way I touch you, my hands on you, God, me inside you, all the things I can't say during the daylight, Tatiana, Tania, Tatiasha, babe, do you feel me?”</i>
</b><br><br>Like I said,this for me the harder book to read of the 3 of them (and that's saying a lot)but I can't separate the books from each other. Reading this series for the first time (I'm sure I'll re-read them several times), was an experience of it's own. It was like reading their memories...not only the memories of several events that change history but the memories of people who lived them. To me they felt real and this story touched my soul. I can't even explain it properly! It's like they're now part of me, if that's make sense.<br><br>Now, I read several reviews that didn't liked this book...that Shura and Tania are barely recognizable and so on. And I agree with several of the points made, there were several times that I felt infuriated, sad, disappointed and even disgusted <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when he was making out with Carmen...I felt sick  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>with some scenes...but i never felt that the "pain" was gratuitous. It was real, it was two young people that lived unbearable and impossible things, trying the best they could to get through it together. To grow together. They make mistakes. They have flaws. They're real.<br><br>Many parts seems the negativity prevails in it but it's because a major part of the book is focused in those earlier years. Like it zoomed in the pivotal moments...but also the happy moments, Antman growing up and his brothers and sister.<br><br>And in the end it's all worthy...every bump in the road made them stronger. And this kind of one of a lifetime love it's all we can aim for. When two souls recognize each other, and from that moment on, they know their fate is irrevocably changed.<br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/268/grm8.jpg/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382616890i/6065269.jpg" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“Do you see the Field of Mars, where I walked next to my bride in her white wedding dress, with red sandals in her hands, when we were kids?”<br><br>“I see it well.”<br><br>“We spent all our days afraid it was too good to be true, Tatiana,” said Alexander. “We were always afraid all we had was a borrowed five minutes from now.”<br><br>Her hands went on his face. “That’s all any of us ever has, my love,” she said. “And it all flies by.”<br><br>“Yes,” he said, looking at her, at the desert, covered coral and yellow with golden eye and globe mallow. “But what a five minutes it’s been.” </i>
</b><br><br><br>True,and reading it" what five minutes it's been"...:)<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7360037060770357038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_954601177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954601177" />
    <a title="Anne OK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/285610-anne-ok"><img alt="Anne OK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505981069p2/285610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954601177?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne OK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne OK" href="/user/show/285610-anne-ok">Anne OK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11196760-the-summer-garden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/285610-anne-ok?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954601177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16012257780390214945">This is no ordinary love story – but one of endless love and devotion and loyalty. It is unforgettable from the very start. Memorable and epic. No other series has ever captured and held me hostage such as Alexander and Tatiana’s beautiful masterpiece of love. It has found its place within the deepest recesses of my heart and soul. <br/><br/>The first two books were my favorites, and although I knew it would take all three to complete the journey, I was less enthused with this last book. <i>The Summer Garden</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16012257780390214945" style="display:none">This is no ordinary love story – but one of endless love and devotion and loyalty. It is unforgettable from the very start. Memorable and epic. No other series has ever captured and held me hostage such as Alexander and Tatiana’s beautiful masterpiece of love. It has found its place within the deepest recesses of my heart and soul. <br /><br />The first two books were my favorites, and although I knew it would take all three to complete the journey, I was less enthused with this last book. <i>The Summer Garden</i> had a different feel and delved into areas where I lost focus and my attention strayed at times. Some of it felt overly repetitious and filled with both unnecessary and unrelated passages in excess that just dragged the story to a slow grind in my opinion. <br /><br />Both <i>The Bronze Horseman</i> and <i>Tatiana and Alexander</i> are masterfully written and powerfully described both the lives of Alexander, the handsome and powerful Red Army officer, and Tatiana, the blonde beauty with a heart of gold, who became the love of Alex's life when he crossed the street for a closer look at a beautiful girl, sitting alone on a bench eating ice cream while waiting for her bus. When the bus arrived, both Alex and Tatiana boarded together and the rest was, as they say, history. Their lives are full of devastation as they go through the atrocities of war where they are faced with uphill battles one after the other. And their love survives it all and on a summer's day in a war torn Russia they marry. The mind is boggled not only by the horrors they face throughout their young lives during wartime, but by their constant love and total commitment to each other even while separated for long spans of time. There’s so much anger, heartbreak, sadness, and loss – but still they find hope. Their love exists no matter what – it’s endless. <br /><br />The wrap-up in the last book devotes itself primarily to Alex and Tatiana’s reunion and healing, finding their place in America and living together as a married couple with the addition of family and friends. It is not always an easy road either. The past has its way of complicating and overshadowing their new life. Happily-ever-after had its moments of darkness and hardships. Even though things seem to be going well for them as homeowners and a home construction business that Alex runs, their marriage is struggling through differences of opinions and jealousies that elicit elements that teeter on infidelity. Frankly, I was sickened to see this kind of behavior dim and discolor the solidarity and certainty in Alex and Tatiana’s love for each other. At this point, I’m questioning why the author felt it necessary. Their relationship had withstood far too much already and to add such sordid blemishes pained me. Even though I blamed Alex and lost respect for my shining hero much more in this area than I did Tatiana, she certainly exacerbated the situation with her stubborn and sometimes wild behavior. With this crisis weathered, time marches on and another challenge presents itself when Alex finds himself thrown into the midst of the Vietnam War when their oldest son is captured and held hostage. And finally, the saga ends with our couple now in the twilight of their lives providing readers with the certainty of happily-ever-afters for the entire Barrington family – but not without a few twists and turns and a surprise or two.<br /><br />I first downloaded this series in 2012. For some unknown reason, I kept putting it aside. I would read a few pages and then set it aside again and again until I finally just gave up. At the dawn of this new year and after being prompted to try once again, I promised and swore that I would not go through another year without reading this series from start to finish. I’ve now completed my self-challenge and can’t help but ask myself why I waited so long. <i>The Bronze Horseman Series</i> is one of the most intense, yet soul touching stories I’ve ever read. It is now etched into my memory. The author is truly gifted in her storytelling and brilliant in her abilities to bring such to life on the pages. If you enjoy a love story of epic proportions, along with unforgettable characters that will hold your heart tightly in its grasp, this series is a must-read. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16012257780390214945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Su/62hBHx6vHFz+3HGqMbsgYXz6n9rOWEe2aiZ8syTRwyZMIqxkOw2A8i9brn4axHke49ml7PfFKk9w4Um87rg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HR9ERRquPpHJ3bxY7X71i5RVyfDG54/Gp8SgLPUTm+snOS2XofD3+W72CDkai/9UQgouOAhqAaH8uuadOFBpcQ==')})
  }

But Nathaniel and Elizabeth Bonner can see that Hannah is not the same woman as when she left. For their daughter has come home without her husband and without her son…and with a story of loss and tragedy that she can’t bear to tell. Yet as Hannah resumes her duties as a gifted healer among the sick and needy, she finds that she is also slowly healing herself. Little does she realize that she is about to be called away to face her greatest challenge ever.As autumn approaches, news of the latest conflict with Britain finds the young men of Paradise—including eighteen-year-old Daniel Bonner—eager to take up arms. Against their better judgment, Nathaniel and Elizabeth must let him go, just as they must let his twin sister Lily, a stubborn beauty, pursue her independence in Montreal. But on the eve of the War of 1812, an unexpected guest arrives from Scotland: It is the Bonners’ distant cousin, the newly widowed Jennet Scott of Carryckcastle. Far from home, Lily and Jennet will each learn the price of pursuing their dreams and the possibility of true love.But it’s Hannah herself who must risk everything once more—this time to save Daniel, who’s been taken prisoner by the British. As the distant thunder of war threatens Paradise, Hannah may learn to live—and maybe love—again in one final act of courage, duty, and sacrifice.A gifted writer, a master storyteller, and a first-rate <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6229852681631651475">Paullina Simons was born in Leningrad, USSR, in 1963. At the age of ten her family immigrated to the United States. Growing up in Russia Paullina dreamt of someday becoming a writer. Her dream was put on hold as she learned English and overcame the shock of a new culture. <br/><br/>After graduating from university and after various jobs including working as a financial journalist and as a translator Paullin</span>
  <span id="freeText6229852681631651475" style="display:none">Paullina Simons was born in Leningrad, USSR, in 1963. At the age of ten her family immigrated to the United States. Growing up in Russia Paullina dreamt of someday becoming a writer. Her dream was put on hold as she learned English and overcame the shock of a new culture. <br /><br />After graduating from university and after various jobs including working as a financial journalist and as a translator Paullina wrote her first novel <i>Tully</i>. Through word of mouth that book was welcomed by readers all over the world. <br /><br />She continued with more novels, including <i>Red Leaves, Eleven Hours, The Bronze Horseman, The Bridge to Holy Cross</i> (also known as <i>Tatiana and Alexander</i>), <i>The Summer Garden</i> and <i>The Girl in Times Square</i> (also known as <i>Lily</i>). Many of Paullina's novels have reached international bestseller lists. <br /><br />Apart from her novels, Paullina has also written a cookbook, <i>Tatiana's Table</i>, which is a collection of recipes, short stories and recollections from her best selling trilogy of novels, <i>The Bronze Horseman, The Bridge to Holy Cross</i>, (also known as <i>Tatiana and Alexander</i>) and <i>The Summer Garden</i>.</span>
